<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funchal">Funchal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Funchal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeira_27_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/260px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/390px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Madeira_27_2014.jpg/520px-Madeira_27_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7303" data-file-height="3651" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeira_27_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Partial view of the capital as seen from the mountains above it</div></div></div>
<p>Funchal is the capital and principal city of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Region">Autonomous Region</a> of Madeira, located along the southern coast of the island of Madeira. It is a modern city, located within a natural geological "<a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">amphitheatre</a>" composed of vulcanological structure and fluvial hydrological forces. Beginning at the harbour (Porto de Funchal), the neighbourhoods and streets rise almost 1,200 metres (3,900&#160;ft), along gentle slopes that helped to provide a natural shelter to the early settlers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Madeira" title="Demographics of Madeira">Demographics of Madeira</a></div>
<p>The island was settled by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese people</a>, especially farmers from the <a href="/wiki/Minho_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Minho (province)">Minho</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> meaning that Madeirans (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Madeirenses</i>), as they are called, are ethnically Portuguese, though they have developed their own distinct regional identity and cultural traits.
</p><p>The region has a total population of just under 270,000, the majority of whom live on the main island of Madeira where the population density is <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="6996337000000000000♠"></span>337/km<sup>2</sup></span>; meanwhile only around 5,000 live on the Porto Santo island where the population density is <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="6996112000000000000♠"></span>112/km<sup>2</sup></span>.
</p><p>About 247,000 (96%) of the population are Catholic and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Funchal" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Funchal">Funchal</a> is the location of the Catholic cathedral.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_diaspora" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese diaspora">Portuguese diaspora</a></div>
<p>Madeirans migrated to the United States, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, British Guiana, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Madeiran immigrants in North America mostly clustered in the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-Atlantic states">mid-Atlantic states</a>, Toronto, Northern California, and Hawaii. The city of <a href="/wiki/New_Bedford" class="mw-redirect" title="New Bedford">New Bedford</a> is especially rich in Madeirans, hosting the Museum of Madeira Heritage, as well as the annual Madeiran and Luso-American celebration, the Feast of the Blessed Sacrament, the world's largest celebration of Madeiran heritage, regularly drawing crowds of tens of thousands to the city's Madeira Field.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg/220px-Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg/330px-Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg/440px-Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg 2x" data-file-width="629" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_immigrant_family_in_Hawaii_during_the_19th_century.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Many <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Americans" title="Portuguese Americans">Portuguese</a> immigrants in <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaii</a> were Madeiran</div></div></div>
<p>In 1846, when a famine struck Madeira over 6,000 of the inhabitants migrated to <a href="/wiki/British_Guiana" title="British Guiana">British Guiana</a>. In 1891 they numbered 4.3% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In 1902 in <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>, Hawaii there were 5,000 Portuguese people, mostly Madeirans. In 1910 this grew to 21,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_Hawaii_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress_Hawaii-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>1849 saw an emigration of Protestant religious exiles from Madeira to the United States, by way of Trinidad and other locations in the West Indies. Most of them settled in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> with financial and physical aid of the American Protestant Society, headquartered in New York City. In the late 1830s the Reverend <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reid_Kalley" title="Robert Reid Kalley">Robert Reid Kalley</a>, from Scotland, a Presbyterian minister as well as a physician, made a stop at Funchal, Madeira on his way to a mission in China, with his wife, so that she could recover from an illness. The Rev. Kalley and his wife stayed on Madeira where he began preaching the Protestant gospel and converting islanders from Catholicism.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, the Rev. Kalley was arrested for his religious conversion activities and imprisoned. Another missionary from Scotland, William Hepburn Hewitson, took on Protestant ministerial activities in Madeira. By 1846, about 1,000 Protestant Madeirenses, who were discriminated against and the subjects of mob violence because of their religious conversions, chose to immigrate to Trinidad and other locations in the West Indies in answer for a call for sugar plantation workers.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The Madeirenses exiles did not fare well in the West Indies. The tropical climate was unfamiliar and they found themselves in serious economic difficulties. By 1848, the American Protestant Society raised money and sent the Rev. Manuel J. Gonsalves, a Baptist minister and a naturalized U.S. citizen from Madeira, to work with the Rev. Arsenio da Silva, who had emigrated with the exiles from Madeira, to arrange to resettle those who wanted to come to the United States. The Rev. da Silva died in early 1849. Later in 1849, the Rev. Gonsalves was then charged with escorting the exiles from Trinidad to be settled in Sangamon and Morgan counties in Illinois on land purchased with funds raised by the American Protestant Society. Accounts state that anywhere from 700 to 1,000 exiles came to the United States at this time.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are several large Madeiran communities around the world, such as the number in the UK, including <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_British" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese British">Portuguese British</a> community mostly made up of Madeirans celebrate <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Day" title="Madeira Day">Madeira Day</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madeira is part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>.
</p><p>The Venezuelan (14.4%), British (14.2%), Brazilian (12.1%) and German (7.0%) nationalities constituted the largest foreign communities residing in the Autonomous Region of Madeira in 2017. The Venezuelan community showed a sharp increase (38.0%). In terms of geographical distribution, it is in Funchal that the foreign population mainly concentrates (59.2% of the total of the Region), followed by Santa Cruz (13.8%), Calheta (7.3%) and Porto Santo (4.0%). The foreign population with resident status in the Autonomous Region of Madeira totaled 6,720 (up by 10.0% from 2016), distributed between residence permits (6,692) and long-stay visas (28).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Madeira_International_Business_Center">Madeira International Business Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Madeira International Business Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canical.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Canical.jpg/220px-Canical.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Canical.jpg/330px-Canical.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Canical.jpg/440px-Canical.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canical.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cani%C3%A7al" title="Caniçal">Caniçal</a> on the left and Madeira Free Trade Zone on the right</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/International_Business_Centre_of_Madeira" title="International Business Centre of Madeira">International Business Center of Madeira</a></div>
<p>The setting-up of a <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Free trade zone">free trade zone</a>, also known as the <a href="/wiki/International_Business_Centre_of_Madeira" title="International Business Centre of Madeira">Madeira International Business Center</a> (MIBC) has led to the installation, under more favorable conditions, of infrastructure, production shops and essential services for small and medium-sized industrial enterprises. The International Business Centre of Madeira comprises presently three sectors of investment: the Industrial Free Trade Zone, the International Shipping Register – MAR and the International Services. Madeira's tax regime has been approved by the European Commission as legal State Aid and its deadline has recently been extended by the E.C. until the end of 2027. The International Business Center of Madeira, also known as Madeira Free Trade Zone, was created formally in the 1980s as a tool of regional economic policy. It consists of a set of incentives, mainly of a tax nature, granted with the objective of attracting inward investment into Madeira, recognized as the most efficient mechanism to modernize, diversify and internationalize the regional economy. The decision to create the International Business Center of Madeira was the result of a thorough process of analysis and study. Other small island economies, with similar geographical and economic restraints, had successfully implemented projects of attraction of foreign direct investment based on international services activities, becoming therefore examples of successful economic policies.
</p><p>Since the beginning, favorable operational and fiscal conditions have been offered in the context of a preferential tax regime, fully recognized and approved by the European Commission in the framework of State aid for regional purposes and under <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">the terms for the Ultra-peripheral Regions</a> set in the Treaties, namely Article 299 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Treaty on European Union">Treaty on European Union</a>. The IBC of Madeira has therefore been fully integrated in the Portuguese and EU legal systems and, as a consequence, it is regulated and supervised by the competent Portuguese and EU authorities in a transparent and stable business environment, marking a clear difference from the so-called "tax havens" and "offshore jurisdictions", since its inception. In 2015, the European Commission authorized the new state aid regime for new companies incorporated between 2015 and 2020 and the extension of the deadline of the tax reductions until the end of 2027. The present tax regime is outlined in Article 36°-A of the Portuguese Tax Incentives Statute. Available data clearly demonstrates the contribution that this development programme has brought to the local economy over its 20 years of existence: impact in the local labor market, through the creation of qualified jobs for the young population but also for Madeiran professionals who have returned to Madeira thanks to the opportunities now created; an increase in productivity due to the transfer of know how and the implementation of new business practices and technologies; indirect influence on other sectors of activity: business tourism benefits from the visits of investors and their clients and suppliers, and other sectors such as real estate, telecommunications and other services benefit from the growth of their client base; impact on direct sources of revenue: the companies attracted by the IBC of Madeira represent over 40% of the revenue in terms of corporate income tax for the Government of Madeira and nearly 3.000 jobs, most of which qualified, among other benefits. Also there are above average salaries paid by the companies in the IBC of Madeira in comparison with the wages paid in the other sectors of activity in Madeira.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_Government">Regional Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Regional Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Madeira has been a significant recipient of <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> funding, totaling up to €2&#160;billion. In 2012, it was reported that despite a population of just 250,000, the local administration owes some €6&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the Portuguese treasury (IGCP) assumed Madeira's debt management between 2012 and 2015. The region continues to work with the central government on a long-term plan to reduce its debt levels and commercial debt stock. Moody's notes that the region has made significant fiscal consolidation efforts and that its tax revenue collection has increased significantly in recent years due to tax rate hikes. Madeira's tax revenues increased by 41% between 2012 and 2016, helping the region to reduce its deficit to operating revenue ratio to 10% in 2016 from 77% in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeira_Beach_(163610932).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/220px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/330px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg/440px-Madeira_Beach_%28163610932%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeira_Beach_(163610932).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Calheta_beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Calheta beach">manufactured coastal beach</a> of <a href="/wiki/Calheta,_Madeira" title="Calheta, Madeira">Calheta</a>: replacing the dark rock/sand of the volcanic island with beach sand.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">Tourism</a> is an important sector in the region's economy, contributing 20%<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> to the region's GDP, providing support throughout the year for commercial, transport and other activities and constituting a significant market for local products. The share in Gross Value Added of hotels and restaurants (9%) also highlights this phenomenon. The island of Porto Santo, with its 9&#160;km (5.6&#160;mi) long beach and its climate, is entirely devoted to tourism.
</p><p>Visitors are mainly from the European Union, with German, British, Scandinavian and Portuguese tourists providing the main contingents. The average annual occupancy rate was 60.3% in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> reaching its maximum in March and April, when it exceeds 70%. 
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Whale_watching">Whale watching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Whale watching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Whale_watching" title="Whale watching">Whale watching</a> has become very popular in recent years. Many species of dolphins, such as <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common dolphin</a>, spotted dolphin, <a href="/wiki/Striped_dolphin" title="Striped dolphin">striped dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short-finned_pilot_whale" title="Short-finned pilot whale">short-finned pilot whale</a>, and whales such as <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale" title="Bryde&#39;s whale">Bryde's whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sei_whale" title="Sei whale">Sei whale</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beaked_whale" title="Beaked whale">beaked whales</a> can be spotted near the coast or offshore.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Electricity on Madeira is provided solely through EEM (Empresa de Electricidade da Madeira, SA, which holds a monopoly for the provision of electrical supply on the autonomous region) and consists largely of fossil fuels, but with a significant supply of seasonal hydroelectricity from the levada system, wind power and a small amount of solar. Energy production comes from conventional thermal and hydropower, as well as wind and solar energy.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The Ribeira dos Soccoridos <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> plant, rated at 15MW utilises a <a href="/wiki/Pumped_hydropower" class="mw-redirect" title="Pumped hydropower">pumped hydropower</a> reservoir to recycle mountain water during the dry summer.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, renewable energy formed 26.5% of the electricity used in Madeira. By 2020, half of Madeira's energy will come from renewable energy sources.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This is due to the planned completion of the Pico da Urze / Calheta <a href="/wiki/Pumped_storage" class="mw-redirect" title="Pumped storage">pumped storage</a> hydropower plant, rated at 30MW.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Battery technologies are being tested to minimize Madeira's reliance on fossil fuel imports.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Renault SA and EEM piloted the Sustainable Porto Santo—Smart Fossil Free Island project on Porto Santo to demonstrate how fossil fuels can be entirely replaced with renewable energy.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Madeira" title="Transport in Madeira">Transport in Madeira</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/220px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/330px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG/440px-Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ve%C4%8Dern%C3%AD_Funchal_z_p%C5%99%C3%ADstavn%C3%ADho_mola.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A ferry makes daily trips between Madeira and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Islands have two airports, <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport">Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo_Airport" title="Porto Santo Airport">Porto Santo Airport</a>, on the islands of Madeira and Porto Santo respectively. From Cristiano Ronaldo International Airport the most frequent flights are to <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>. There are also direct flights to over 30 other airports in Europe and nearby islands.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Transport between the two main islands is by plane, or ferries from the Porto Santo Line,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> the latter also carrying vehicles. Visiting the interior of the islands is now easy thanks to construction of the <i>Vias Rápidas</i>, major roads that cross the island. Modern roads reach all points of interest on the islands.
</p><p>Funchal has an extensive public transportation system. Bus companies, including <a href="/wiki/Hor%C3%A1rios_do_Funchal" title="Horários do Funchal">Horários do Funchal</a>, which has been operating for over a hundred years, have regularly scheduled routes to all points of interest on the island.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Madeira" title="Music of Madeira">Music of Madeira</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeirenses.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/220px-Madeirenses.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/330px-Madeirenses.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Madeirenses.jpg/440px-Madeirenses.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Madeirenses.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bailinho da Madeira</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">Folklore</a> music in Madeira is widespread and mainly uses local musical instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Machete_(musical_instrument)" title="Machete (musical instrument)">machete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rajao" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajao">rajao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brinquinho" title="Brinquinho">brinquinho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cavaquinho" title="Cavaquinho">cavaquinho</a>, which are used in traditional folkloric dances like the <i>bailinho da Madeira</i>.
</p><p>Emigrants from Madeira also influenced the creation of new musical instruments. In the 1880s, the <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">ukulele</a> was created, based on two small guitar-like instruments of Madeiran origin, the <a href="/wiki/Cavaquinho" title="Cavaquinho">cavaquinho</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rajao" class="mw-redirect" title="Rajao">rajao</a>. The ukulele was introduced to the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a> by <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> immigrants from Madeira and Cape Verde.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Three immigrants in particular, Madeiran cabinet makers Manuel Nunes, José do Espírito Santo, and Augusto Dias, are generally credited as the first ukulele makers.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Two weeks after they disembarked from the <i><a href="/wiki/Ravenscrag_(ship)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ravenscrag (ship)">SS Ravenscrag</a></i> in late August 1879, the <i>Hawaiian Gazette</i> reported that "Madeira Islanders recently arrived here, have been delighting the people with nightly street concerts."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/220px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/330px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg/440px-Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patella_vulgata_Madeira_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>"Lapas", the true limpet species <i><a href="/wiki/Patella_vulgata" title="Patella vulgata">Patella vulgata</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Because of the geographic situation of Madeira in the Atlantic Ocean, the island has an abundance of fish of various kinds. The species that are consumed the most are espada (<a href="/wiki/Black_scabbardfish" title="Black scabbardfish">black scabbardfish</a>), <a href="/wiki/Thunnus" title="Thunnus">blue fin tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_marlin" title="White marlin">white marlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_blue_marlin" title="Atlantic blue marlin">blue marlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albacore" title="Albacore">albacore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bigeye_tuna" title="Bigeye tuna">bigeye tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wahoo" title="Wahoo">wahoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">spearfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_tuna" title="Skipjack tuna">skipjack tuna</a> and many others are found in the local dishes as they are found up and down the coast of Madeira.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Espada is often served with banana. <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">Bacalhau</a> is also popular, as it is in Portugal.
</p><p>There are many meat dishes on Madeira, one of the most popular being <a href="/wiki/Espetada" title="Espetada">espetada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Espetada is traditionally made of large chunks of beef rubbed in garlic, salt and bay leaf and marinated for 4 to 6 hours in Madeira wine, red wine vinegar and olive oil then skewered onto a <a href="/wiki/Bay_laurel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay laurel">bay laurel</a> stick and left to grill over smouldering wood chips. These are so integral a part of traditional eating habits that a special iron stand is available with a T-shaped end, each branch of the "T" having a slot in the middle to hold a <a href="/wiki/Brochette" class="mw-redirect" title="Brochette">brochette</a> (espeto in Portuguese); a small plate is then placed underneath to collect the juices. The brochettes are very long and have a V-shaped blade in order to pierce the meat more easily. It is usually accompanied with the local bread called <a href="/wiki/Bolo_do_caco" title="Bolo do caco">bolo do caco</a>.
</p><p>Other popular dishes in Madeira include <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7orda" title="Açorda">açorda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">feijoada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carne_de_Vinha_d%27_Alhos" class="mw-redirect" title="Carne de Vinha d&#39; Alhos">carne de vinha d'alhos</a>.
</p><p>Traditional pastries in Madeira usually contain local ingredients, one of the most common being <i>mel de cana</i>, literally "sugarcane honey" (<a href="/wiki/Molasses" title="Molasses">molasses</a>). The traditional cake of Madeira is called <i><a href="/wiki/Bolo_de_Mel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolo de Mel">Bolo de Mel</a></i>, which translates as (Sugarcane) "Honey Cake" and according to custom, is never cut with a knife, but broken into pieces by hand. It is a rich and heavy cake. The cake commonly well known as "<a href="/wiki/Madeira_cake" title="Madeira cake">Madeira cake</a>" in England also finds its naming roots in the Island of Madeira.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Malasada" title="Malasada">Malasadas</a> are a Madeiran creation that were taken around the world by emigrants to places such as Hawaii. In Madeira, <a href="/wiki/Malasada" title="Malasada">Malasadas</a> are mainly consumed during the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Madeira" title="Carnival of Madeira">Carnival of Madeira</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pastel_de_nata" title="Pastel de nata">Pastéis de nata</a>, as in the rest of Portugal, are also very popular.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Milho_Frito" class="mw-redirect" title="Milho Frito">Milho Frito</a> is a very popular dish in Madeira that is very similar to the Italian dish <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>. <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A7orda" title="Açorda">Açorda</a> Madeirense is another popular local dish.
</p><p>The island of Madeira is famous for the quality of its <a href="/wiki/Cherimoya" title="Cherimoya">Cherimoya</a> fruits.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The Annona Festival is traditional and occurs annually in the parish of Faial. This event encourages the consumption of this fruit and its derivatives, such as liqueurs, puddings, ice cream and smoothies.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beverages">Beverages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Beverages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Madeira_wine" title="Madeira wine">Madeira wine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/220px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/330px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG/440px-Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vino_D_Oliveiras.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bottles of Madeira labelled by the different grape varieties used to produce the many styles of wine</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:114px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CORAL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7f/CORAL.jpg" decoding="async" width="112" height="314" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="112" data-file-height="314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CORAL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coral Beer, produced since 1872<sup id="cite_ref-ecm.pt_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecm.pt-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> in the Island's main brewery, has achieved several <a href="/wiki/Monde_Selection" title="Monde Selection">Monde Selection</a> medals</div></div></div>
<p>Madeira is a <a href="/wiki/Fortified_(wine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortified (wine)">fortified wine</a>, produced in the Madeira Islands; varieties may be sweet or dry. It has a history dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Exploration" class="mw-redirect" title="Age of Exploration">Age of Exploration</a> when Madeira was a standard <a href="/wiki/Port#Port_of_call" title="Port">port of call</a> for ships heading to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> or <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>. To prevent the wine from spoiling, neutral <a href="/wiki/Grape_spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="Grape spirit">grape spirits</a> were added. However, wine producers of Madeira discovered, when an unsold shipment of wine returned to the islands after a round trip, that the flavour of the wine had been transformed by exposure to heat and movement. Today, Madeira is noted for its unique winemaking process that involves heating the wine and deliberately exposing the wine to some levels of <a href="/wiki/Oxidation" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxidation">oxidation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sotheby_pg_340–341_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sotheby_pg_340–341-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Most countries limit the use of the term <i>Madeira</i> to those wines that come from the Madeira Islands, to which the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> grants <a href="/wiki/Protected_designation_of_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected designation of origin">Protected designation of origin</a> (PDO) status.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A local beer called Coral is produced by the <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Brewery" title="Madeira Brewery">Madeira Brewery</a>, which dates from 1872. It has achieved 2 <a href="/wiki/Monde_Selection" title="Monde Selection">Monde Selection</a> Grand Gold Medals, 24 Monde Selection Gold Medals and 2 Monde Selection Silver Medals.<sup id="cite_ref-ecm.pt_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecm.pt-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Other alcoholic drinks are also popular in Madeira, such as the locally created <a href="/wiki/Poncha" title="Poncha">Poncha</a>, Niquita, Pé de Cabra, Aniz, as well as Portuguese drinks such as <a href="/wiki/Macieira_Brandy" title="Macieira Brandy">Macieira Brandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Licor_Beir%C3%A3o" title="Licor Beirão">Licor Beirão</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Laranjada" title="Laranjada">Laranjada</a> is a type of <a href="/wiki/Carbonation" title="Carbonation">carbonated</a> soft drink with an orange flavour, its name being derived from the Portuguese word <i>laranja</i> ("orange"). Launched in 1872 it was the first soft drink to be produced in Portugal, and remains very popular to the present day. <a href="/wiki/Brisa_drink" title="Brisa drink">Brisa drinks</a>, a brand name, are also very popular and come in a range of flavours.
</p><p>There is also a huge <a href="/wiki/Coffee_culture" title="Coffee culture">coffee culture</a> in Madeira. Like in mainland Portugal, popular coffee-based drinks include <a href="/wiki/Garoto_Coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Garoto Coffee">Garoto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A3o" title="Galão">Galão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bica_Coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Bica Coffee">Bica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_com_Cheirinho" class="mw-redirect" title="Café com Cheirinho">Café com Cheirinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazagran_(coffee_beverage)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazagran (coffee beverage)">Mazagran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinesa" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinesa">Chinesa</a> and many more.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Madeira" title="Sport in Madeira">Sport in Madeira</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_provinces">Sister provinces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sister provinces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Madeira Island has the following sister provinces:
</p>
<ul><li>Italy: <a href="/wiki/Aosta_Valley" title="Aosta Valley">Autonomous Region of Aosta Valley</a> (1987)</li>
<li>Jersey: <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Jersey" class="mw-redirect" title="Bailiwick of Jersey">Bailiwick of Jersey</a> (1998)</li>
<li>South Africa: <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Cape_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Cape Province">Eastern Cape Province</a></li>
<li>South Korea: <a href="/wiki/Jeju_Province" title="Jeju Province">Jeju Province</a> (2007)</li>
<li>Gibraltar: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> (2009)<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Postage_stamps">Postage stamps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Postage stamps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamps_and_postal_history_of_Madeira" title="Postage stamps and postal history of Madeira">Postage stamps and postal history of Madeira</a></div>
<p>Portugal has issued postage stamps for Madeira during several periods, beginning in 1868.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madeira&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal,_10th_June_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/170px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/255px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg/340px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal%2C_10th_June_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2810" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_-_Croatia_vs._Portugal,_10th_June_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, born in Madeira, was the 2008, 2013, 2014, 2016 and 2017 <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d&#39;Or">World Player of the Year</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joe_berardo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/170px-Joe_berardo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/255px-Joe_berardo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Joe_berardo.jpg/340px-Joe_berardo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2896" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Joe_berardo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Joe_Berardo" title="Joe Berardo">Joe Berardo</a> is a businessman, <a href="/wiki/Stock_investor" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock investor">stock investor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speculator" class="mw-redirect" title="Speculator">speculator</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_collector" class="mw-redirect" title="Art collector">art collector</a>. He is also one of the wealthiest people in Portugal.</div></div></div>
<p>The following people were either born or have lived part of their lives in Madeira:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Austria" title="Charles I of Austria">Charles I of Austria</a>, last <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Austria" title="Emperor of Austria">Emperor of Austria</a> and last <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">King of Hungary</a>, deposed monarch, died in exile on Madeira in 1922</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="António de Abreu">António de Abreu</a>, naval officer and navigator</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miguel_Albuquerque" title="Miguel Albuquerque">Miguel Albuquerque</a>, third and current President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nadia_Almada" title="Nadia Almada">Nadia Almada</a>, a winner of the British reality show <a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_2004_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Brother 2004 (UK)">Big Brother</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Berardo" title="Joe Berardo">Joe Berardo</a>, Portuguese millionaire, and art collector</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rubina_Berardo" title="Rubina Berardo">Rubina Berardo</a>, Portuguese politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Menasseh_Ben_Israel" title="Menasseh Ben Israel">Menasseh Ben Israel</a>, Jewish rabbi.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jaime_Ornelas_Camacho" title="Jaime Ornelas Camacho">Jaime Ornelas Camacho</a>, <i>first and former</i> President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_Camacho" title="Pedro Camacho">Pedro Macedo Camacho</a>, composer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catarina_Fagundes" title="Catarina Fagundes">Catarina Fagundes</a>, Olympic athlete for <a href="/wiki/Windsurf" class="mw-redirect" title="Windsurf">windsurf</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/V%C3%A2nia_Fernandes" title="Vânia Fernandes">Vânia Fernandes</a>, Portuguese singer who represented Portugal in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurovision 2008">Eurovision 2008</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vicente_de_Freitas" title="José Vicente de Freitas">José Vicente de Freitas</a>, military general and politician</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama_Rodrigues" title="Vasco da Gama Rodrigues">Vasco da Gama Rodrigues</a>, poet, born in <a href="/wiki/Paul_do_Mar" title="Paul do Mar">Paul do Mar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Teod%C3%B3sio_Clemente_de_Gouveia" class="mw-redirect" title="Teodósio Clemente de Gouveia">Teodósio Clemente de Gouveia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinal of the Roman Catholic Church</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Walter_Grabham" title="George Walter Grabham">George Walter Grabham</a>, geologist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herberto_H%C3%A9lder" title="Herberto Hélder">Herberto Hélder</a>, poet</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Henriques" class="mw-redirect" title="Moisés Henriques">Moisés Henriques</a>, former Australian Under-19 Captain and current <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_cricket_team" title="New South Wales cricket team">NSW Blues</a> and Australian international <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> cricketer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alberto_Jo%C3%A3o_Jardim" title="Alberto João Jardim">Alberto João Jardim</a>, second President of the Regional Government</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Jardim" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Jardim">Luís Jardim</a>, producer of music</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Langerhans" title="Paul Langerhans">Paul Langerhans</a>, German <a href="/wiki/Pathologist" class="mw-redirect" title="Pathologist">pathologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biologist" title="Biologist">biologist</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/F%C3%A1tima_Lopes" title="Fátima Lopes">Fátima Lopes</a>, fashion designer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Tolentino_Mendon%C3%A7a" title="José Tolentino Mendonça">José Tolentino Mendonça</a>, priest, theologian, poet, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishop</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aires_de_Ornelas_e_Vasconcelos" title="Aires de Ornelas e Vasconcelos">Aires de Ornelas e Vasconcelos</a>, former Archbishop of the former Portuguese colonial enclave <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> (in India)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Mathews" title="Lloyd Mathews">Lloyd Mathews</a>, British naval officer, politician and abolitionist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pestana_Group" title="Pestana Group">Dionísio Pestana</a>, president of the <a href="/wiki/Pestana_Group" title="Pestana Group">Pestana Group</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rigo_23" title="Rigo 23">Rigo 23</a>, artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Rodrigues_(sailor)" title="João Rodrigues (sailor)">João Rodrigues</a>, Olympic <a href="/wiki/Windsurfer" class="mw-redirect" title="Windsurfer">windsurfer</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, professional footballer for <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Santos" class="mw-redirect" title="John Santos">John Santos</a>, photographer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ana_da_Silva" title="Ana da Silva">Ana da Silva</a>, founding member of <a href="/wiki/Post-punk" title="Post-punk">post-punk</a> band <a href="/wiki/The_Raincoats" title="The Raincoats">The Raincoats</a></li>
<li>Manoel Dias Soeyro or <a href="/wiki/Menasseh_Ben_Israel" title="Menasseh Ben Israel">Menasseh Ben Israel</a> (1604–1657), <a href="/wiki/Spanish_and_Portuguese_Jews" title="Spanish and Portuguese Jews">Sephardi</a> <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">rabbi</a> and publisher</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Sousa" title="Bernardo Sousa">Bernardo Sousa</a>, rally driver in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rally_Championship" title="World Rally Championship">WRC</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Artur_de_Sousa_Pinga" class="mw-redirect" title="Artur de Sousa Pinga">Artur de Sousa Pinga</a>, former <a href="/wiki/CS_Mar%C3%ADtimo" class="mw-redirect" title="CS Marítimo">CS Marítimo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Futebol_Clube_do_Porto" class="mw-redirect" title="Futebol Clube do Porto">FC Porto</a> football player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maximiano_de_Sousa_(Max)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximiano de Sousa (Max)">Maximiano de Sousa (Max)</a>, popular singer, born in <a href="/wiki/Funchal" title="Funchal">Funchal</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virg%C3%ADlio_Delgado_Teixeira" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgílio Delgado Teixeira">Virgílio Teixeira</a>, actor</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Travassos_Valdez,_1st_Count_of_Bonfim" title="José Travassos Valdez, 1st Count of Bonfim">José Travassos Valdez, 1st Count of Bonfim</a>, governor during 1827–1828</li></ul>
